CONSENT CALENDAR
All matters listed under the Consent Calendar are considered to be routine and will be enacted by one motion without discussion. If
discussion is desired, that item may be removed and considered separately.
 
1.
Planning Commission 2026 Regular Meeting Calendar – Adoption
Adopt the Planning Commission Regular Meeting schedule for the calendar year 2026.
CEQA: This action is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that
will not result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)
PUBLIC COMMENT
During the public comment period, members of the public may speak on general items of interest within the Commission's
jurisdiction that are not on the agenda.  Each member of the public may speak for a maximum of three minutes with a maximum of
15 minutes for the entire public comment period. The Chair shall determine whether the matter is within the Commission's
jurisdiction. The Commission shall not act on or discuss any matters raised during the public comment period, which are not on the
agenda, but shall refer such matters to staff for review and/or request such matters be placed on a future agenda.
PUBLIC HEARING
Planning Commission decisions are final unless appealed to the City Council in accordance with Section 27.08.090 and Section
27.08.060 of the San Mateo Municipal Code. The time within which judicial review of any final decision may be sought is governed by
Code of Civil Procedure section 1094.6. If any person challenges a Planning action in court, they may be limited to raising only those

--- page 2 ---
issues raised at the public hearing or in written correspondence delivered to the City of San Mateo, at or prior to, the public hearing.
Some public hearings will be automatically referred to City Council and those will be indicated below.
 
2.
430 Station Park Circle - Station Park Green Specific Area Plan Amendment (PA-2025-048)
Recommend to the City Council adoption of a resolution to amend the Station Park Green Specific Plan and
Station Park Green Design Guidelines to change the mix of floor area allowed for retail and office uses, and adopt
an addendum to the Initial Study/Mitigated Negative Declaration pursuant to California Environmental Quality
Act Sections 15162 and 15164, based on the Findings for Approval and subject to the Conditions of Approval.
CEQA: A Mitigated Negative Declaration (MND) for the Station Park Green Specific Plan was certified by the City
Council on January 28, 2011. An addendum to the MND was provided for the application that was approved in 2014
(PA-2014-055). The findings for approval for this project include environmental findings that rely on the previously
certified MND, which tiered off of the San Mateo Rail Corridor Transit-Oriented Development Plan (Corridor Plan)
Environmental Impact Report (EIR) (certified in 2010). 
The amendments to the Specific Plan will not result in any new impacts or increase the severity of any impacts
previously identified in the MND because the updated use ranges allowed for the ground floor of Building MU-1 are
within the ranges for office and retail uses that were originally studied and allowed in the Specific Plan adopted in
2011. Therefore, no additional environmental documentation is necessary pursuant to CEQA Guidelines Section
15162 and 15164 because there are no substantial changes in the project; no new information of substantial
importance, which was not known and could not have been known with the exercise of reasonable diligence at the
time the previous IS/MND was certified; or no substantial evidence in the record revealing that there have been
substantial changes with respect to the circumstances under which the project is undertaken. As such, an Addendum
to the MND has been prepared (Attachment 11). The proposed changes are not substantial in scope under CEQA
Sections 15162 and 15164 as determined by the lead agency in accordance with CEQA Section 15064(f)7.

SUBJECT:
430 Station Park Circle - Station Park Green Specific Area Plan Amendment (PA-2025-048) 
RECOMMENDATION:
Recommend to the City Council adoption of a resolution to amend the Station Park Green Specific Plan and Station Park 
Green Design Guidelines to change the mix of floor area allowed for retail and office uses, and adopt an addendum to the 
Initial Study/Mitigated Negative Declaration pursuant to California Environmental Quality Act Sections 15162 and 15164, 
based on the Findings for Approval and subject to the Conditions of Approval.
BACKGROUND:
In 2011, the City Council approved the Station Park Green Specific Plan and the Station Park Green Design Guidelines, and 
adopted an Initial Study/Mitigated Negative Declaration (PA-2007-030).  In 2014, the City Council approved a Specific Plan 
amendment and a formal application for a Site Plan & Architectural Review (SPAR), Site Development Permit (SDP), and 
Parcel Map to modify this mixed-use development (PA-2014-055).  Additionally, a modification to the previously approved 
SPAR application was approved in 2020 in order to remove stairs within a required PG&E easement (PA-2020-061). 
The Station Park Green Specific Plan is a transit-oriented mixed-use development, located in the San Mateo Rail Corridor 
Transit Oriented Development (TOD) Zoning District near the Hayward Park Caltrain Station. The site is approximately 12-
acres (521,396 square feet)  and includes four buildings with 599 residential units, a 3,000 square-foot community room and 
36,000 square feet of office and retail uses, and a 2.3-acre park. Building MU-1, which is located at the corner of S. Delaware 
Street and Concar Drive, is the only mixed-use building with four upper stories of residential uses and 36,058 square feet of 
ground-level space (excluding parking and mechanical areas) for office and retail uses. 
Since project completion in 2018, the property owner has reported that the retail spaces in the MU-1 building have been  
challenging to lease.  The last operating business (a sandwich shop) located at the corner of S. Delaware Street and Concar 
Drive closed recently, and most retail spaces have never been occupied. The applicant stated that for seven years they have 
worked with brokers to find tenants for the retail spaces, but have not been able to find prospective businesses. Thus, the 
applicant is requesting an amendment to the Specific Plan and Design Guidelines to allow these ground floor retail spaces 
to be occupied with office uses.  The Draft Resolution with the requested amendments to allow for ground floor office uses 
is included in Attachment 1.
Project Description and Modifications
The project proposes amending the existing Specific Plan and Design Guidelines to convert the majority of existing ground 
floor retail spaces into office space within MU-1 Building. The current Specific Plan and Design Guidelines encourage active 
retail uses and have a minimum requirement of 25,000 square feet of retail/services/restaurant use. The reduction of retail 
requires an amendment to the program (see table below with calculations of existing and proposed retail and office space

--- page 7 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
square footage).  The proposed project consists of interior modifications to ground floor uses as detailed in the table below.
Table 1 – Proposed square footage by use

No change
Building MU-1 is bounded by S. Delaware Street, Concar Drive, Station Park Circle, and Green Way.  The building is five levels 
and consists of retail and office space on the ground floor with four levels of residential apartment units above. The applicant 
proposes relocating the community room and retail spaces to the southeast side of the building along Concar Drive, with 
office spaces placed along the other three sides of the building to improve connectivity and tenant circulation.  The proposed 
plans are included as Attachment 3 and the plans from the previous amendment in 2014 are included as Attachment 4.   The 
building’s total square footage would remain the same. A location map showing the project site, its vicinity, and adjacent 
zoning designations is included as Attachment 5. 
The applicant also proposes minor exterior site improvements, including new furniture, lighting, and landscaping along the 
project’s street frontages on Concar Drive and S. Delaware Street, and design and landscaping improvements to the plaza 
space at the corner of Concar and Delaware to make it more inviting and accessible for pedestrians. 
To support these requested changes in uses, the applicant has provided a retail viability report prepared by the Econic 
Company (Attachment 2), which outlines the significant challenges in finding retails tenants for these existing spaces, 
including a lack of retail synergy with the immediate area, wider economic factors (such as online shopping) and the lack of 
clearly visible storefront parking. The applicant cites these issues as reasons why potential retail tenants do not open shops 
in Station Park Green, even with rental concessions. The City’s retail consultant, Retail Real Estate Resources (RRER), also 
reviewed this application and provided input and recommendations (Attachment 6).  Generally, RRER agreed that these 
attributes have had a negative impact on rental feasibility, but recommends that the existing restaurant space (Space I on 
the plan set) that has had infrastructure installed be preserved for retail uses along with the adjacent space to create retail 
synergy, as well as improving the visibility of storefront signage.  RRER recommends that the majority of the ground floor 
spaces be allowed to be used as office space, or quasi-retail for a non-profit or similar use, to support its ability to be 
occupied.  To support longer-term economic development strategies and to avoid losing all of this retail space to office uses, 
the City has included a requirement that a minimum of 3,000 square feet of floor area be preserved for retail uses. Condition 
of Approval #3 requires the applicant to commit to investments that make the space more viable for businesses to lease 
these spaces and to rent reductions.
While the mix of uses on the ground floor of MU-1 will change, the existing on-and-off-street parking layout with 932 parking 
spaces will not change. Since office space requires less parking than retail, the proposed project will be providing more 
parking than is required. Hexagon Transportation Consultants, Inc. provided a trip generation report stating that the 
proposed conversion from retail to office uses would generate up to 197 fewer daily trips (Attachment 7). Additionally, as 
the project is within one-half mile of Hayward Park Caltrain Station, additional parking for residential and commercial uses 
is not required pursuant to Assembly Bill (AB) 2097.  The project also does not impact bicycle parking, as sufficient short- 
and long-term bike parking spaces are provided for the office and retail uses.    
Additionally, as part of this application, the applicant has offered to provide a community benefit in the form of a $50,000 
contribution toward neighborhood park improvements at Concar Park and Sunnybrae Park.  Additional information about 
this contribution is included in the Applicant Cover Letter in Attachment 2. These funds will support the City’s efforts to 
enhance public parks and community amenities.
Attachment 8 provides comprehensive tables that list proposed modifications to the Station Park Green Specific Plan and 
Design Guidelines. The previously approved Specific Plan and Design Guidelines are included as Attachment 9. Details on the

--- page 8 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
findings for approval are included in the Draft Resolution (Attachment 1).
APPLICABLE CODE AND POLICY REVIEW:
General Plan and Zoning Map Amendment
The General Plan 2040 Land Use Map designates the project site as Mixed-Use Medium II. The Mixed-Use Medium II land 
use designation was established to provide for medium-density mixed-use buildings that provide a variety of commercial, 
office, and/or residential uses within the same site or building. Since General Plan 2040 land use designation of Mixed-Use 
Medium II allows for offices, the proposed amendment would be consistent with the General Plan. 
The property is in the San Mateo Rail Corridor Transit Oriented Development (TOD) Zoning District. Furthermore, the site is 
within the Hayward Park Station TOD Overlay Zone. This zone allows for multi-family residential development with 
community-serving ground floor retail uses. The intention of the ground floor retail in this area is to provide shops, 
restaurants, and personal services for commuters and neighborhood. The Hayward Park TOD Overlay Zone also allows for 
some office, but with a preference for ground floor retail and services. The proposed amendment would expand the amount 
of office space permitted in the zone, in particular on the ground floor. 
In the Station Park Green Specific Plan and Design Guidelines, ground floor retailers are encouraged in Building MU-1 to face 
the streets (S. Delaware Street and Concar Drive) as well as the public plaza and greenway. Offices are a permitted land use 
under the Specific Plan, and the Design Guidelines state that offices (along with retail/services/restaurants) shall be the 
primary use in Building MU-1; however, the increase in offices would affect the program requirement of maintaining a 
minimum of 25,000 square feet of retail space. 
The specific plan amendment is consistent with state housing laws, and there is no net loss in residential capacity. The 
proposed specific plan amendment also does not involve a decrease in the allowable building height, maximum allowable 
density, or floor area ratio (FAR); nor would it increase requirements for lot size, setbacks, or other development 
requirements or standards that would lessen the intensity of housing.
PUBLIC COMMENTS:
The applicant held a formal Neighborhood Informational Meeting on March 19, 2025. The applicant’s summary of the 
neighborhood meeting is included as Attachment 10. The meeting was attended by 18 guests. 
Under the provisions of Government Code Section 65352.3, Tribal Consultation Notices were sent on July 23, 2025, with a 
deadline to respond by October 19, 2025. No tribal consultation requests were received. 
NEXT STEPS:
Following a Planning Commission recommendation on the proposed Specific Plan and Design Guidelines Amendments, the 
project will be scheduled for a City Council public hearing for formal action on this Planning Application.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
A Mitigated Negative Declaration (MND) for the Station Park Green Specific Plan was certified by the City Council on January 
28, 2011. An addendum to the MND was provided for the application that was approved in 2014 (PA-2014-055).  The findings 
for approval for this project include environmental findings that rely on the previously certified MND, which tiered off of the 
San Mateo Rail Corridor Transit-Oriented Development Plan (Corridor Plan) Environmental Impact Report (EIR) (certified in 
2010).  
The amendments to the Specific Plan will not result in any new impacts or increase the severity of any impacts previously 
identified in the MND because the updated use ranges allowed for the ground floor of Building MU-1 are within the ranges 
for office and retail uses that were originally studied and allowed in the Specific Plan adopted in 2011. Therefore, no 
additional environmental documentation is necessary pursuant to CEQA Guidelines Section 15162 and 15164 because there 
are no substantial changes in the project; no new information of substantial importance, which was not known and could 
not have been known with the exercise of reasonable diligence at the time the previous IS/MND was certified;  or no 
substantial evidence in the record revealing that there have been substantial changes with respect to the circumstances

--- page 9 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
under which the project is undertaken.  As such, an Addendum to the MND has been prepared (Attachment 11).  The 
proposed changes are not substantial in scope under CEQA Sections 15162 and 15164 as determined by the lead agency in 
accordance with CEQA Section 15064(f)7.

Attachment 1 – Draft Resolution with Findings
CITY OF SAN MATEO
DRAFT RESOLUTION 
RESOLUTION OF THE PLANNING COMMISSION RECOMMENDING APPROVAL OF AN AMENDMENT TO THE 
STATION PARK GREEN SPECIFIC PLAN AND STATION PARK GREEN DESIGN GUIDELINES (PA-2025-048) TO 
REDUCE THE AMOUNT OF REQUIRED RETAIL SPACE AND INCREASE THE AMOUNT OF REQUIRED OFFICE SPACE 
AT 430 STATION PARK CIRCLE (APN 035-200-180 AND 035-200-060)
WHEREAS, on January 18, 2011, the City Council approved Planning Application (PA) 2007-030 for a 
Specific Plan, Design Guidelines, and Development Agreement to allow for the construction of 599 residential 
units, 10,000 to 45,000 square feet of office uses, and 25,000 to 60,000 square feet of retail uses within the 
Hayward Park Station Transit Oriented Development (TOD) Area in the San Mateo Rail Corridor Transit Oriented 
Development Plan at 430 Station Park Circle (APN 035-200-180 and 035-200-060); and 
WHEREAS, on February 2, 2015, the City Council approved PA 2014-055 for a Specific Plan amendment, 
amendments to the Design Guidelines, a Site Plan and Architectural Review for a mixed-use development, site 
development approval, a vesting tentative parcel map, and an Addendum to the Original Mitigated Negative 
Declaration; and 
WHEREAS, the Specific Plan and Design Guidelines amendments required a minimum of 25,000 square 
feet for retail/service/restaurant uses and a maximum of 15,000 square feet for office uses; and
WHEREAS, the site is currently developed with four five-story buildings, with Building MU-1 containing 
residential, commercial, and retail uses; and
WHEREAS, in recent years the property owner has been unsuccessful in finding and maintaining retail 
tenants at this location; and
WHEREAS, on May 29, 2025, the applicant submitted PA 2025-048 to change the Specific Plan and 
Design Guidelines to decrease retail space (from 25,034 square feet to 7,298 square feet), increase office space 
(from 7,991 square feet to 25,639 square feet), and increase of amenity space (from 3,031 square feet to 3,122 
square feet); while not modifying the overall structure square footage, height, setbacks, lot size, or parking of 
Building MU-1; and
WHEREAS, the Project is consistent with the applicable policies of the General Plan and other applicable 
codes and policies; and 
WHEREAS, on October 28, 2025, the Planning Commission held a duly noticed public hearing, at which 
time the Commission _____.

--- page 11 ---
NOW, THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, BY THE PLANNING COMMISSION OF THE CITY OF SAN MATEO, 
CALIFORNIA, HEREBY FINDS AND RESOLVES THAT:
1.
The Planning Commission recommends that the City Council finds on the basis of the whole record 
before it that there is no substantial evidence that the Project will have a significant effect on the 
environment. In accordance with CEQA Section 15162.b, subsequent environmental review is not 
required because the project is consistent with the development density established by the City’s 
General Plan 2040 policies for which an Environmental Impact Report (EIR) was certified on March 18, 
2024. The Addendum to the Mitigated Negative Declaration, originally adopted on February 2, 2015, 
is still accurate because there are no proposed addition or exterior modification to the existing 
structures; there are no project specific effects which are peculiar to the project or its site; there are 
no project specific impacts which the General Plan Update EIR failed to analyze as significant effects; 
there are no potentially significant off-site and cumulative impacts which the General Plan EIR failed 
to evaluate; and there is no substantial new information which results in more severe impacts than 
anticipated by the general plan EIR. Furthermore, any future development of the site would be subject 
to a project specific environmental assessment consistent with the CEQA statues and guidelines in 
effect at that time. 
 
2.
The Planning Commission recommends that the City Council approve the project based on findings 
and subject to the conditions of approval attached hereto as Exhibit A and incorporated by 
reference is upheld.  
3.
The Station Park Green Specific Plan and Design Guidelines (PA-2025-048) is recommended for 
approval based on the analysis of the Project as a whole and substantial evidence in the record, and 
based upon the findings and conditions of approval included in Exhibit A, attached hereto and 
incorporated by reference.
4.
The project conforms to the following Land Use Policies and Community Design and Historic Resources 
Policies of the City’s General Plan 2040: 
a.
Policy LU 3.2 Commercial Development. Encourage development that builds on the strengths 
and unique qualities of existing neighborhoods and provides appropriate transition in terms of 
intensity of use, height, bulk, and design. Require commercial development adjacent to 
residential areas to appropriately address circulation, traffic, truck loading, trash/recycling, noise, 
visual impacts, public safety, hazardous materials storage, fire safety, air pollutant emissions, and 
odors in a way that minimizes impacts on neighboring uses. 
b.
Policy LU 3.10 Office Park Evolution. Support the transition of single-use office parks into mixed-
use districts that include residential, retail, office, services, and/or parks and open space. Within 
an office site that is redeveloping as mixed-use, locate offices and commercial space closest to 
high-volume roadways and locate new residential uses and outdoor spaces as far as possible from 
high-volume roadways.

--- page 12 ---
c.
Policy LU 3.9 Workplaces. Develop office buildings and business parks to facilitate transit, 
pedestrian, and bicycle commutes. Provide compact development, mixed uses, and connectivity 
to transit to reduce vehicle miles traveled (VMT). 
d.
Policy CD 8.2 Human-Scale Design. Cultivate pedestrian activity in commercial and mixed-use 
areas by providing adequate sidewalk widths, activating ground-floor street façades with active 
uses, windows, plantings, and awnings, using high-quality construction materials, and including 
human-scale details and architectural features. 
The project conforms to these policies in that the proposed office spaces is within an existing 
structure, does not increase negative impacts to adjacent residential uses, and is located next to busy 
roadways. The offices are located within a half-mile of the Hayward Park Caltrain station, and the 
development already provides sufficient vehicle and bicycle parking for employees. The proposed 
modifications to the public plazas will enhance pedestrian activity on the site. The project is located 
in the San Mateo TOD zoning district and Mixed-Use Medium II area per the General Plan’s Land Use 
Plan and is consistent with the applicable subdivision and zoning code standards, including minimum 
lot sizes, building height, and floor area ratio, as outlined in the findings above. In addition to the new 
conditions placed upon the application, all other conditions in the prior Planning Application remain 
in effect.

The following conditions of approval apply to the project referenced above. The conditions of 
approval are grouped under specific headings that relate to the timing of required compliance. 
Additional language within a condition may further define the timing of required compliance. 
The following conditions shall be satisfied prior to issuance of any BUILDING PERMITS, or prior to 
the deadline specified in that condition.
Planning Division (PA)
1 ACTIVE CORNER – The applicant shall submit a plan to enhance the corner plaza as an 
active space for pedestrians and visitors. The plan shall provide details that shows how the 
site will engage with the adjacent building and surrounding neighborhood, and include 
elevations showing the interaction between the modified walls, windows and doors 
adjacent to the plaza. The plaza design is subject to review and approval by Planning staff 
as part of the building permit. 
2
3
COMMUNITY ROOM – The Applicant shall develop, operate, and maintain a community 
space of at least 3,000 square feet that is available to the City community free of charge by 
reservation and subject to availability. The Community Room shall meet the requirements 
listed in the Condition of Approval from PA-2014-055 (Condition 57.d), include signage that 
meets the standards in the Station Park Green Storefront Guidelines, and maintain a 
reservation/booking system to support community access consistent with City 
requirements. The Community Room design is subject to review and approval by Planning 
staff as part of the building permit.
BUILDING MU-1 GROUND FLOOR USES – The ground floor of the MU-1 Building is

RE: StaƟon Park Green Speciﬁc Plan Amendment ApplicaƟon – Allow some exisƟng retail space to be 
used as oﬃce 
 
Dear Planning Commission Members, 
 
My name is Chris Kober, and I am the Vice President of Redevelopment for Essex.  I am wriƟng to you 
today to both explain our applicaƟon that is coming to your Commission and to ask for your support of 
it. 
 
In 2018 our company completed the construcƟon of StaƟon Park Green, a new community located 
adjacent to the Hayward Park CalTrain staƟon.  There are 599 apartment homes at the community, 
arranged around a nice public park.  The residenƟal community has been home to thousands of San 
Mateo residents over these years and is in high demand as it is consistently occupied at 95% or higher.   
By contrast, the ground ﬂoor retail porƟon of the community has not succeeded. The extensive eﬀorts to 
ﬁnd tenants for the retail spaces at SPG have not been successful in the 7-year life of the community. As 
a result, the majority of the retail spaces are vacant and have never been occupied. Numerous retail 
brokers have been working to ﬁnd businesses to occupy the retail, but despite reaching out to over 1,400 
potenƟal users, the site has proven to not be a suitable one for most users. The vacant retail (along 
Delaware and Concar) has created an empty and “closed” feeling within the greater community and 
along the pedestrian pathways (including those leading to the train staƟon). Professional retail brokers 
with the Econic Company and Newmark Realty have been working on this project for years.  They 
produced a report of the inability to have sustainable retail here at this project. The city staﬀ engaged 
their own retail expert, and they conﬁrmed the diﬃculƟes of having that much retail space at SPG. 
 
As a result, this project applicaƟon seeks to amend the Speciﬁc Plan and the Design Guidelines to allow 
some of the exisƟng long-vacant retail space to be used instead as oﬃce space. That new oﬃce use will 
house a new corporate headquarters oﬃce for our company, Essex Property Trust (the owner of SPG). 
Essex, a Fortune 500 public company, is currently headquartered in San Mateo. Our current space lease 
is coming to an end. Essex wants to conƟnue in San Mateo (and not move to another city) and have our 
oﬃces be relocated to SPG. No new space will be created with this project. The applicaƟon is to merely 
change the allowable use of a porƟon of the already exisƟng building. Once that use is allowed, some 
tenant improvement work will be conducted to ﬁt out our new oﬃce. Our headquarters oﬃce will have 
capacity of up to 75-100 Essex employees, although the actual occupancy on any given day will be less 
than that, as many Essex employees are out in the ﬁeld working. All the necessary parking already exists 
in oﬀ-street parking garages.   The retail expert hired by the city came to the same conclusion that a 
reducƟon in retail space was the right direcƟon.

Uses of Spaces (Suites A, I and J) at Station Park Green 
October 16, 2025 
 
Retail 
In an effort to help attract neighborhood serving retailers, and to support their ongoing 
success, the Owner will work with prospective retailers to help them to locate at Station 
Park Green.  The intent is to emphasize coffee and light food retailers, whose hours of 
operation (throughout the workday) are supportive of the train station commuters and 
office workers in the area as well as the residents in the surrounding neighborhoods.  It is 
further desired to have experienced retailers, with previous operating experience, good 
credit and liquidity, with the goal that the retail succeeds and stays in business.  The Owner 
will assist potential retail tenants in suites A, I and J with tenant improvement funds and 
discounted rent according to the attached Exhibit A. 
Non-Proﬁt Office Space (Suite A only) 
For suite A, the space could be considered for use as a non-proﬁt organization’s office 
space, instead of retail.   Local non-proﬁts struggle to ﬁnd affordable space within the 
community to operate, and this transit adjacent location could potentially be a good ﬁt for 
that use.  If the City desires to have this suite used in this fashion, the Owner will work with 
the non-proﬁt office user to provide tenant improvement funds and discounted rent 
according to the attached Exhibit A.

--- page 21 ---
Exhibit A – Speciﬁc Incentives to Promote Retail (or Non-proﬁt Use) 
 
Retail (Suites A, I and J) 
• Work with the City and Economic Development Department to solicit the type of 
retailers that will best suit the community and have a reasonable chance of 
success. 
• Offer Tenant Improvement funds on a one-time basis on a standard lease term (10 
years) to assist the start-up of those desired retailers: 
o Depending upon use, up to $80/ square foot for the currently unﬁnished and 
never occupied spaces (suites A and I) 
o Depending upon use, up to $60/ square foot for the previous Starbuck’s 
space which has some improvements already (suite J) 
o Provide 6 months of free rent to help get the retailers established and 
develop their customer base 
• These incentives are conditioned upon retailers complying with the community’s 
standard lease, insurance and credit requirements. 
 
Non- Proﬁt Office Use Alternative (for Suite A only) 
• Work with the City to identify speciﬁc non-proﬁt(s) that would be most desirable for 
space that do not conﬂict with the existing residential community  
• Would dedicate a limited amount of reserved parking (5 spaces in ground ﬂoor 
garage) for office users, with heavy reliance on public transit for workers 
• Offer Tenant Improvement funds on a one-time basis on a standard lease term to 
assist the start-up of the desired non-proﬁt: 
o Depending upon use, up to $30/ square foot  
o Provide 6 months of free rent to help get the non-proﬁt established (with an 
average lease in the $21/ foot range) 
• These incentives are conditioned upon a non-proﬁt complying with the community’s 
standard lease, insurance and credit requirements.

Project Description 
 
Community 
 
Station Park Green (SPG) is a mixed-use community in San Mateo that contains 599 homes, a 
public park and ground ﬂoor retail and oƯice spaces. The community is adjacent to the Hayward 
Park CalTrain station. SPG was constructed in 2018, and its development was covered by the 
Station Park Green Speciﬁc Plan and the Station Park Green Design Guidelines, which were 
enacted by the City Council in 2011. The Speciﬁc Plan was in keeping with the broader San Mateo 
Rail Corridor Transit-Oriented Development Plan (the “Rail Corridor Plan”), which was approved by 
the City Council on June 6, 2005. As part of that approval in 2011, the city certiﬁed in 2010 an Initial 
Study/Mitigated Negative Declaration that tiered oƯ the Rail Corridor Plan EIR. 
 
Failure of Retail 
 
After the construction was complete the residential portion of SPG has successfully operated and 
been home to thousands of San Mateo residents. By contrast, the retail portion of the community 
has not succeeded. The extensive eƯorts to ﬁnd tenants for the retail spaces at SPG have not been 
successful in the 7-year life of the community. As a result, the majority of the retail spaces are 
vacant and have never been occupied. Numerous retail brokers have been working to ﬁnd 
businesses to occupy the retail, but despite reaching out to over 1,400 potential users, the site has 
proven to not be a suitable one for most users. The vacant retail (along Delaware and Concar) has 
created an empty and “closed” feeling within the greater community and along the pedestrian 
pathways (including those leading to the station). Professional retail brokers with the Econic 
Company and Newmark Realty have been working on this project for years.  They produced a report 
of the inability to have sustainable retail here at this project. That report is being submitted as part 
of the application. 
 
Proposed Project to Revitalize Vacant Retail into New OƯice 
 
As a result, this project application seeks to amend the Speciﬁc Plan and the Design Guidelines to 
allow some of the long-vacant retail space to be used as oƯice space. That new oƯice use will 
house a new corporate headquarters oƯice for Essex Property Trust (the owner of SPG). Essex, a 
Fortune 500 public company, is currently headquartered in San Mateo. The current space lease is 
coming to an end. Essex wants to continue in San Mateo and have its oƯices be relocated to SPG. 
No new space will be created with this project. The application is to merely change the allowable 
use of a portion of the already existing building. Once that use is allowed, some tenant

--- page 23 ---
2 
 
improvement work will be conducted to ﬁt out the new oƯice. That headquarters oƯice will have 
capacity of up to 75-100 Essex employees, although the actual occupancy on any given day will be 
less than that, as many Essex employees are out in the ﬁeld working. All the necessary parking 
already exists in oƯ-street parking garages.  
 
Remaining Retail 
 
Some of the existing neighborhood serving retail space will be retained along the pedestrian 
corridor parallel to Concar Drive. These are the spaces with the most retail potential as they have 
good walk by traƯic and street visibility.   Speciﬁcally the plan will have: 
 
One retail space at the corner of Delaware and Concar.  This retail use will have outside 
dining potential in the existing public plaza.  To help support that retail, the corner plaza will 
be enhanced to really accentuate it as a gateway to the community.  New seating and string 
lighting will help promote longer retail hours for the beneﬁt of the train commuters and 
community at large. 
 
Another retail space along Concar at the signalized intersection of Concar and the Highway 
92 ramps.  This corner retail location will have great visibility to street traƯic and also will 
serve those pedestrians on the path to the train station. 
 
Between these two retail spaces we will relocate the Community Room, which is available 
for all San Mateo residents to host events or group meetings. 
 
The positioning of these retail and community areas will create a block of community 
activity in one location.  This remaining retail will also be supported by the new Essex 
employees that come to work each day and help with the retailers’ breakfast and lunch 
operations. 
 
Special eƯort and outreach will be conducted to attract local business operators to these 
spaces to provide desirable food and retail uses that best serve the neighborhood. 
 
Beneﬁts of the Project 
 
 
Currently vacant ground ﬂoor spaces will be occupied, creating a more vibrant 
environment. The retail spaces have been vacant for 7 years and would likely continue that 
way into the future without a change in use. Having people in these spaces will activate the 
street scene and make the pedestrian pathway experience to the train station more 
enjoyable. Speciﬁcally, the sidewalk areas along Delaware and Concar will receive 
upgrades with benches, landscaping and lighting. 
 
The existing pedestrian pathway from Delaware to the public park inside SPG will be 
enhanced. Landscape upgrades, seating and string lights will provide a pleasant route 
throughout the day, inviting more community to use the park. 
 
The newly located Community Room within SPG will be available for San Mateo resident 
use for functions and meetings free of charge. There will be furnished conference and 
meeting spaces as well as a kitchen area for group use. The space can be reserved for use 
by contacting the community. 
 
The presence of oƯice employees will help support the neighborhood retail spaces such as 
food and coƯee shop uses. The hope is that the increased customer base will allow the 
retailers to be open for longer hours and be more successful.


As part of Essex’s ongoing commitment to San Mateo, as part of this application we will be
working with the City and the Mayor’s oƯice on a contribution for potential upgrades to the
neighborhood parks (Concar and Sunnybrae).
Speciﬁc Plan Amendment Process and Speciﬁcs 
A Speciﬁc Plan Amendment and Design Guidelines Amendment application is being ﬁled with the 
City of San Mateo, and those amendments must be approved by the Planning Commission and the 
City Council through public hearings. A requirement of submitting the application for an 
amendment is to hold a Neighborhood Meeting with the neighboring residents of SPG. We held that 
Public Meeting via Zoom on March 19th, 2025. The recording of that meeting, including questions 
raised and participants, is part of the application. We expect to process the amendments during 
2025. 
What Will Change in the Speciﬁc Plan and Design Guidelines 
The amendment will modify some speciﬁc language in the Speciﬁc Plan and the Design Guidelines 
as to the minimum and maximum amounts of space that may be used for retail and for oƯice.

TraƯic Impact of Change of Use 
 
As part of the original design and construction of SPG, the third-party traƯic consultant, Hexagon 
produced a traƯic study which encompassed all the residential, retail and oƯice uses. For this 
application, once the City’s Transportation Engineer conﬁrms the work scope, Hexagon will be 
producing an updated traƯic study showing retail space conversion to oƯice. The major points 
related to traƯic are: 
 
There were more traƯic trips anticipated with retail use than the proposed oƯice use. 
 
The location of SPG adjacent to the Highway 92 ramps allows for easy commuter ingress 
and egress without disruption to neighborhood streets. 
 
Essex employees already utilize CalTrain for commuting purposes, and this new proximity 
will enhance that usage, reducing car trips.

City of San Mateo 
Via Email 
Re: 
Ground Floor Commercial Space 
Station Park Green 
430 Station Park Circle 
San Mateo, CA 
To whom it may concern, 
 
We are the leasing team assigned with procuring tenants for the ground floor commercial spaces located 
within the Station Park Green project.  The Econic Company is a specialized retail real estate firm 
focusing on bringing our expertise to both landlords and tenants against an ever-changing retail and 
economic landscape. We have decades of market specific experience representing landlords in San 
Mateo County, and have been very active with similar mixed-use projects.  We have represented many of 
the major multifamily companies including Essex Property Trust, Fairfield Residential, Prometheus, 
Avalon Bay, Equity Residential, Brookfield and a variety of local and regional groups.  Many of these 
projects have been leased to 100% occupancy and have successful retail components. 
 
My team and I have been working on leasing these spaces since 2017, the first six years under 
Newmark, and the past two years under The Econic Company.  Through both brokerage firms, our 
leasing team has struggled greatly to attract any interested tenants for the ground floor spaces.     
 
The biggest hurdle to achieving successful retail at this property is the lack of retail synergy in the 
immediate area.  Most retailers look for clusters of co-tenancy to provide proven sales records and 
existing customer traffic.  As the retail world has become increasingly more difficult over the last ten years 
due to the rise of online sales, retail tenants are more cautious than ever and have been reluctant to enter 
unproven trade areas.  The presence of nearly 600 residential units on site certainly does provide some 
level of customer base, but it is almost insignificant in the eyes of retailers who are looking at the total 
demographics within a 3 to 5 mile radius of the project.  We have had several tenants who’ve had active 
requirements in San Mateo in the past, and ultimately decided to locate either downtown San Mateo or 
along El Camino Real in the area surrounding Hillsdale Shopping Center.  One such tenant was 
Clayroom, a pottery studio company based in San Francisco that had 3 locations in 2022 and was looking 
to expand into San Mateo.  Essex was willing to drop their rent to 50% of previous targets for this tenant, 
but ultimately there were no economic concessions that could overcome the tenant’s concerns over the 
attributes of the project.  They signed a lease at Bay Meadows, surrounded by hundreds of thousands of 
square feet of existing retail and restaurants, ensuring strong customer traffic. 
 
In addition to major constraints surrounding the location of the project in relation to existing clusters of 
retail and consumer traffic, there are physical challenges that have hampered leasing efforts to date.  
There are no convenient street front parking spaces available directly in front of the majority of the retail 
units.  In addition there are not open surface parking lots in front of any of the retail, which is another key 
to success with many retailers.  In a denser market like San Francisco this is less of an issue, but in a 
suburban neighborhood it is a major impediment to retail leasing.  Visibility and street presence are also 
key to retail success.  This site suffers from many issues along these lines.  Some spaces have next to no 
visibility, and signage is very limited as well.

--- page 28 ---
We have paid a premium to upgrade our online listing presence for Station Park Green on LoopNet, 
CoStar, Crexi and the other major commercial real estate listing platforms.  In addition to the broad 
marketing efforts which include regular outreach to commercial real estate brokers throughout the bay 
area, we have reached out individually to over 1,400 local and regional tenants specifically for Station 
Park Green.  The list of retail users we have approached is attached to this letter.  The tenant community 
has voiced their concerns over the viability of a wide range of tenant categories at this project.  We have 
offered very aggressive economic terms and still have been unable to attract interested retail and service 
businesses.  Starbucks signed a ten year lease for this site and ended up closing their café permanently 
after trying to find success here.  They opened in 2019 and closed permanently in 2021.  I Love 
Kickboxing opened in 2019 and closed their doors permanently in 2023.   
 
We feel strongly that there are inherent problems with the retail layout that cannot be remedied as we 
outlined above.  These issues have led to the vacancy ever since the project opened in 2018.  As such, 
the long vacant retail would likely remain empty into the future.  The best solution to the ongoing vacancy 
issues at this project would be to retain the two retail/restaurant units at the hard corner of Delaware & 
Concar, as these could find users, but to convert the other shell spaces into another use such as office.  
This would activate the entire ground floor of the project and bring much needed foot traffic to support the 
existing deli and a future coffee or restaurant tenant in the former Starbucks space.  This would achieve a 
much more stable balance between office and retail at the project and would allow ownership to focus on 
supporting the reduced retail which would have the hard corner visibility to hopefully thrive in the future.   
 
Yours sincerely, 
 
 
 
Matt Sweeney  
 
 
 
Sean O’Carroll  
Executive Director

ZONING:
TOD DISTRICT (TRANSIT ORIENTED DEVELOPMENT PER SAN MATEO MUNI. CODE SEC. 27.90)
PROJECT ADDRESS:
TBD (CORNER OF SOUTH DELAWARE STREET AND CONCAR DRIVE)
PROJECT SUMMARY:
THE PROJECT CONSISTS OF FOUR INDIVIDUAL BUILDINGS ON A ~12 ACRE SITE. OF THE FOUR
BUILDINGS, ONE IS A MIXED-USE BUILDING WITH RETAIL AND OFFICE SPACE ON THE FIRST
FLOOR AND FOUR STORIES OF RESIDENTIAL UNITS ABOVE. THE REMAINING THREE
BUILDINGS ARE COMPOSED ENTIRELY OF RESIDENTIAL UNITS. THE PROJECT PROVIDES
STUDIO, 1-BEDROOM, 2-BEDROOM AND 3-BEDROOM UNITS FOR A TOTAL UNIT COUNT OF 599.
EACH BUILDING CONTAINS A CONCEALED PARKING GARAGE CORE OF TYPE 1A
CONSTRUCTION AROUND WHICH THE RESIDENTIAL PORTIONS (OF TYPE IIIA AND VA
CONSTRUCTION) ARE "WRAPPED." OVER TWO ACRES OF PARK OPEN SPACE ARE INCLUDED
IN THE PROJECT.
SITE AREA:
11.97 ACRES (521,396 SF)
OPEN SPACE:
2.3 ACRES (102,292 SF)
DENSITY:
599 UNITS / 11.97 ACRES = 50 DU/AC
F.A.R.:
2.3
STRUCTURAL SYSTEM:
GARAGES, TYPE IA - CAST IN PLACE CONCRETE AND CONCRETE MASONRY UNITS ON A MAT
FOUNDATION.
RETAIL/ OFFICE, TYPE IA - CONCRETE COLUMNS AND PODIUM DECK SUPPORTING LEVELS
ABOVE, WHERE APPLICABLE.
RESIDENCES, TYPE VA AND IIIA - WOOD STUD BEARING WALLS, POSTS AND BEAMS. FIRE-
RETARDANT-TREATED WOOD USED WHERE REQUIRED FOR TYPE IIIA CONSTRUCTION.
MIXED USE:
IN ADDITION TO 599 RESIDENTIAL UNITS, THE PROJECT CONSISTS OF THE FOLLOWING USES:
OFFICE SPACE:
10,755 S.F.
RETAIL SPACE:
27,784 S.F.
AMENITIES SPACE:
7,649 S.F.

Concar Ranch and Enterprises, Inc., San Mateo, California, being a portion of Parcel "B" as recorded in
Parcel Map Book 16 at Page 21, Official Records of San Mateo County, being also a portion of the lands
conveyed to Concar Ranch Enterprises, Inc., by Deed recorded in Volume 3249 of Official Records of San
Mateo County at Page 703, which said Parcel Map was recorded June 13, 1973 in Parcel Map Book 21 at
Page 8 in the Office of the Recorder of County of San Mateo, State of California.

feet and a central angel of 93*40'17", an arc distance of 24.52 feet to a line parallel with and distant 37.00

said South Delaware Street, thence Southeasterly along the Northwesterly line of said Street South 41*28'
East 125.00 feet to the true point beginning.

NOTES:
1.
THE SPECIFIC PLAN AND DESIGN GUIDELINES FOR STATION PARK GREEN DO NOT REQUIRE TRADITIONAL SETBACKS FROM THE PROPERTY
LINE. INSTEAD, THE INTERFACE BETWEEN EACH BUILDING AND STREET IS CONTROLLED BY A "BLOCK LINE" SET AT THE BACK OF THE
SIDEWALK. WHERE A BUILDING DOES NOT FRONT ON A STREET (NORTH OF BUILDING RE-4 AND ALONG THE EVAE), THE SPECIFIC PLAN DOES
NOT REQUIRE A SETBACK, THOUGH BUILDINGS ARE HELD A REASONABLE DISTANCE AWAY FROM THE PROPERTY LINE.
2.
THE RELATIONSHIP BETWEEN THE BUILDINGS NUMBERED AND NAMED ON THIS SITE PLAN AND THE "BLOCKS" DESIGNATED IN THE SPECIFIC
PLAN AND DESIGN GUIDELINES IS AS FOLLOWS:
BLOCK 1 = BUILDING MU-1
BLOCK 2 = BUILDING RE-2
BLOCK 3 = BUILDING RE-3
BLOCK 4 = BUILDING RE-4
3.
PER VESTING TENTATIVE MAP INCLUDED AS SHEET V 1.0 IN THIS PLAN PACKAGE, THE PROPERTY IN QUESTION CURRENTLY CONSISTS OF TWO
PARCELS, APNs 035-200-006 AND 035-200-180. THE PROJECT PROPOSES TO MERGE THE TWO PARCELS AND RE-PARCEL THE ENTIRE ~11.97
ACRES OF LAND INTO 4 PARCELS, DESIGNATED AS PARCELS 1 THROUGH 4 ON THE PROPOSED VESTING TENTATIVE MAP ON SHEET V 1.1.

PARKING NOTES:
Consistent with the Rail Corridor Plan, Station Park Green will be a transit-oriented development. During the first phase of Station Park Green,
the goal is to create 25% fewer new vehicle trips than would be expected using standard Institute of Transportation Engineers (ITE)
projections. (Conditions of Approval & Mitigation Monitoring Program, pp. 21-22.) At full build-out, the target is a 26% to 36% trip reduction
from ITE standards. (Id., p. 22.)
Parking:
The Applicant proposes to provide off-street parking for the various uses at Station Park Green collectively at the site. This means that some
parking spaces used by dwelling units, or non-residential tenants, may not necessarily be located within the same block as the user to which
it is assigned.
As to residential parking, the Applicant proposes to provide one (1) assigned parking space per dwelling unit within the same block as that
unit.  All other residential parking spaces will be pooled.  Each lease for a dwelling unit will include only one assigned parking space.
Residents may, if they wish, enter into a separate agreement to reserve additional parking spaces from the pool.  The total number of
residential spaces (both those assigned to specific units, and pooled) is 781, and they are provided and highlighted in YELLOW on this
parking plan per the table labeled "Parking Provided - Residential."
Each lease to non-residential tenants will include only as many parking spaces as must be assigned to such tenant based upon parking
standards set by the Specific Plan.  In total, 131 parking spaces will be provided for non-residential uses, and they are provided and
highlighted in VIOLET on this parking plan per the table labeled "Parking Provided - Non-Residential (All)."
Shared Parking:
These 131 non-residential spaces will be used by the non-residential tenants (including 20 office space tenants), and, as analyzed in a
shared parking study by the City’s consultant, will also be made available for use by residential visitors.  It is anticipated that these spaces will
be used by residential visitors primarily during non-business hours.
During SPAR, the City may consider allowing required off-street parking stalls serving any uses, whether residential or non-residential, to be
space-efficient, without the need for a variance. (Specific Plan, p. 119.) Space-efficient could mean stackers, valet, compact spaces, or
other methods. At this time, the Applicant is not proposing any space-efficient parking, pending further review and refinement of its
application.
Car Sharing:
The Applicant plans to provide at least one car-sharing stall for every 230 required off-street motor vehicle parking stalls. “Car-sharing” means
a service that provides an integrated network of neighborhood-based automobiles available only to members by reservation for periods as
short as one hour. (Design Guidelines, p. 107.) Proposed locations for five (5) car-sharing stalls are provided and highlighted in BLUE on
this parking plan per the table labeled "Parking Provided - Non-Residential (All)."
Loading:
Loading facilities will comply with Sections 27.64.310 through 27.64.390 of the San Mateo Municipal Code. However, during SPAR, the City
may consider allowing required loading facilities to be located on-street, without the need for a variance. (Specific Plan, p. 119.) Loading
facilities are provided and highlighted in GREEN on this parking plan per the table labeled "Parking Provided - Non-Residential (All).".
Bicycles:
Station Park Green encourages pedestrians and bicyclists, and provides non-motorized access to all parts of the Plan Area. (Design
Guidelines, p. 105.) To support bicyclists, the Applicant proposes to provide bicycle parking facilities in an amount equal to at least five
percent (5%) of the required number of off-street motor vehicle parking stalls, as required by the Specific Plan. The total required number of
such spaces is 42 (778 + 57 = 835 *.05), and 43 spaces are provided, labeled "Short Tem Bicycle Parking" and highlighted in RED on this
parking plan per the table labeled "Bicycle Parking - Non-Residential." These spaces are designated for public use, and are distributed
around the site as shown. In addition, the owner intends to provide additional secured bicycle storage for Tenant use in each of the building
garages.

NARRATIVE:
BUILDING RE-4 IS A MIXED OCCUPANCY BUILDING COMPRISED OF A TYPE IA 5-STORY
GARAGE CORE WRAPPED BY A 5 STORY TYPE IIIA MULTI-FAMILY RESIDENCE.
AUTOMATIC FIRE SPRINKLERS ARE USED TO ALLOW A HEIGHT INCREASE FOR THE TYPE IIIA
PORTION IN ACCORDANCE WITH SECTION 504.2.
ALL RESIDENTIAL UNITS AND THE CIRCULATION SPACES SERVING THEM ARE ACCESSIBLE
PER CBC CHP. 11A. ALL NON-RESIDENTIAL SPACES ARE ACCESSIBLE PER CBC CHP. 11B.
3-HR RATED FIRE WALLS ARE USED TO SEPARATE THE GARAGE FROM THE SURROUNDING
TYPE IIIA RESIDENCE AS WELL AS TO SUBDIVIDE THE RESIDENCE INTO ALLOWABLE AREAS IN
COMPLIANCE WITH TABLE 503.

SECTION 708.13 - REFUSE AND LAUNDRY CHUTES
(LAUNDRY CHUTES NOT PROVIDED. REFUSE AND RECYCLING ONLY)
708.13.1 REFUSE AND LAUNDRY CHUTE ENCLOSURES - "Openings into the shaft, including those from
access rooms and termination rooms, shall be protected... Openings into chutes shall not be located in
corridors."
708.13.3 REFUSE AND LAUNDRY CHUTE ACCESS ROOMS - "Access openings... shall be located in
rooms or compartments enclosed by not less than 1-hour fire barriers... or horizontal assemblies. Openings...
shall be protected by opening protectives... of not less than 3/4-hour."
708.13.4 TERMINATION ROOM - "Refuse and laundry chutes shall discharge into an enclosed room
separated from the remainder of the building by not less than 1-hour fire barriers... or horizontal assemblies.
Openings... shall be protected by opening protectives... of not less than 3/4-hour."
708.13.6 AUTOMATIC SPRINKLER SYSTEM - "An approved automatic sprinkler system shall be installed in
accordance with Section 903.2.11.2."
SNAPSHOT:
TABULAR ALLOWABLE AREA (At) = 24,000 SF (NOTE: (At) = (Aa) NO AREA MODIFICATIONS ARE
APPLIED)
TOTAL ALLOWABLE BUILDING AREA = (Aa)x2 (48,000 SF W/ MODIFICATION PER SEC 506.4.1)
ALLOWABLE AREA PER FLOOR = 48,000/5 = 9,600 SF
NUMBER OF STORIES = 4 (5 W/ MODIFICATION PER SEC 504)
HEIGHT IN FEET = 65' (85' W/ MODIFICATION PER SEC 504)
SECTON 503 - GENERAL BUILDING HEIGHT AND AREA LIMITATIONS
SEC 503.1.2 BUILDINGS ON SAME LOT - "Two or more buildings on the same lot shall be regulated as
separate buildings or shall be considered as portions of one building..." THE GARAGE AND RESIDENCE
PORTIONS ARE OF DIFFERENT CONSTRUCTION TYPES AND SHALL BE REGULATED AS SEPARATE
BUILDINGS.
TABLE 503 - ALLOWABLE BUILDING HEIGHTS AND AREAS
TYPE IIIA, R-2 OCCUPANCY GROUP: 4 STORIES, 65' HEIGHT & At = 24,000 SF.
SECTION 504 - BUILDING HEIGHT
SEC 504.2 AUTOMATIC SPRINKLER SYSTEM INCREASE - "Where a building is equipped throughout with
an automatic sprinkler system... maximum building height is increased by 20 feet and the maximum number
of stories is increased by one. In other than Group... R occupancies... these increases are permitted in
addition with Section 506.3" AUTOMATIC SPRINKLER SYSTEM INCREASE IS APPLIED TO BUILDING
HEIGHT AND MAY NOT BE USED TO ALLOW AN AREA INCREASE SINCE THE BUILDING IS OF TYPE
IIIA CONSTRUCTION.
SECTION 506 - BUILDING AREA MODIFICATIONS
SEC 506.2 FRONTAGE INCREASE - NOT USED
SEC 506.3 AUTOMATIC SPRINKLER SYSTEM INCREASE - USED FOR HEIGHT INCREASE
SEC 506.4 (506.4.1) SINGLE OCCUPANCY BUILDINGS WITH MORE THAN ONE STORY - "For Group... R
occupancies... the total allowable area of a single occupancy building with more than one story above grade
plane shall be determined by multiplying the allowable area per story (Aa)... by the number of stories above
grade plan as listed below: 1. For buildings with two or more stories above grade plane, multiply by 2; 2. No
Story shall exceed the allowable building area per story (Aa) as determined in Section 506.1..."  TOTAL
ALLOWABLE BUILDING AREA IS CALCULATED AS 2x(Aa).
Aa = [At + (At x If) + (At x Is)]
Aa = 24,000 SF + (24,000 SF x 0) + (24,000 SF x 0)]
Aa = 24,000 SF
(Aa)x2 = 48,000 SF
SECTION 508 - MIXED USE AND OCCUPANCY
SEC 508.2 ACCESSORY OCCUPANCIES - "Accessory occupancies are those occupancies that are
ancilary to the main occupancy of the building or portion thereof." SEE SHEETS A0-3.X FOR OCCUPANCY
CLASSIFICATIONS OF INDIVIDUAL SPACES, CALCULATION OF ACCESSORY (508.2) AND
INCIDENTAL ACCESSORY OCCUPANCIES (508.2.5)
SEC 508.2.1 AREA LIMITATIONS - "Aggregate accessory occupancies shall not occupy more than 10
percent of the building area of the story in which they are located..."
SEC 508.2.5 SEPARATION OF INCIDENTAL ACCESSORY OCCUPANCIES - "The incidental accessory
occupancies listed in Table 508.2.5 shall be separated from the remained of the building or equipped with an
automatic fire-extinguishing system, or both, in accordance with Table 508.2.5"
SEC 508.4 SEPARATED OCCUPANCIES - SEE "OCCUPANCY SEPARATIONS," THIS SHEET.
SECTION 509.5 - GROUP R-1 AND R-2 BUILDINGS OF TYPE IIIA CONSTRUCTION
NOT USED
SECTION 602 - CONSTRUCTION CLASSIFICATION
TABLE 601 - FIRE-RESISTANCE RATING REQUIREMENTS FOR BUILDING ELEMENTS - SEE "FIRE-
RESISTANCE RATING REQUIREMENTS FOR BUILDING ELEMENTS (TABLE 601)," THIS SHEET.
SECTION 706 - FIRE WALLS
SEC 706.1 GENERAL - "Each portion of a building separated by one or more fire walls that comply with the
provisions of this section shall be considered a separate building." THE S-2 GARAGE BUILDING IS
SEPARATED FROM THE R-2 RESIDENCE BUILDING BY FIRE WALLS WHICH ARE ALSO LOAD-
BEARING WALLS AND HAVE A 3-HOUR FIRE-RESISTANCE RATING IN ORDER TO MEET THE
REQUIREMENTS OF TABLE 602. ADDITIONALLY, THE R-2 PORTIONS OF THE BUILDING ARE
SUBDIVIDED BY FIRE WALLS TO CREATE SEPARATE "BUILDINGS."
SECTION 706.2 STRUCTURAL STABILITY - "Fire Walls shall have sufficient structural stability under fire
conditions to allow collapse of construction on either side without collapse..."
SEC 706.5 HORIZONTAL CONTINUITY - "Fire Walls shall be continuous from exterior wall to exterior wall...
Exceptions: 3. Fire Walls shall be permitted to terminate at the interior surface of noncombustible exterior
sheathing where the building on each side of the fire wall is protected by an automatic sprinkler system..."
BUILDINGS SHALL BE PROTECTED THROUGHOUT WITH AN NFPA 13 AUTOMATIC SPRINKLER
SYSTEM AND FIRE WALLS SHALL TERMINATE AT THE INTERIOR SURFACE OF NONCOMBUSTIBLE
EXTERIOR SHEATHING.
SEC 706.6 VERTICAL CONTINUITY - "Fire Walls shall extend from the foundation to a termination point at
least 30 inches above both adjacent roofs. Exceptions: 4. In buildings of Type III, IV, and V construction,
walls shall be permitted to terminate at the underside of combustible roof sheathing or decks, provided..."
FIRE WALLS SHALL TERMINATE AT THE UNDERSIDE OF COMBUSTIBLE ROOF SHEATHING IN
COMPLIANCE WITH EXCEPTION 4.
SECTION 706.8 OPENINGS - "Each opening through a Fire Wall shall be protected in accordance with
Section 715.4 and shall not exceed 156 square feet. The aggregate width of openings at any floor level shall
not exceed 25% of the length of the wall."
SECTION 707 - FIRE BARRIERS
SEC 707.3.1 SHAFT ENCLOSURES - see 708.4
SEC 707.3.2 EXIT ENCLOSURES - see 1022.1
SEC 707.3.3 EXIT PASSAGEWAY - see 1023.3
SEC 707.3.4 HORIZONTAL EXIT - N/A
SEC 707.3.5 ATRIUMS - N/A
SEC 707.3.6 INCIDENTAL ACCESSORY OCCUPANCIES - see 508.2.5
SEC 707.6 OPENINGS - "Openings in a fire barrier shall be protected in accordance with Section 715.
Openings in a fire barrier shall be limited to a maximum aggregate width of 25% of the length of the wall and
the maximum area of any single opening shall not exceed 156 sf. Openings in exit enclosures and exit
passageways shall also comply with Sections 1022.3 and 1023.5, respectively."
SEC 708 (708.2) SHAFT ENCLOSURES - "Openings through a floor/ceiling assembly shall be protected by
a shaft enclosure complying with this section."
SECTION 903 - AUTOMATIC SPRINKLER SYSTEMS
SEC 903.3.1.1 NFPA 13 SPRINKLER SYSTEMS - "Where the provisions of this code require that a building
or portion thereof be equipped throughout with an automatic sprinkler system in accordance with this
section, sprinklers shall be installed throughout in accordance with NFPA 13..." ALL BUILDINGS WILL BE
EQUIPPED THROUGHOUT WITH AUTOMATIC SPRINKLER SYSTEMS PER NFPA 13.
SNAPSHOT:
TABULAR ALLOWABLE AREA (At) = UNLIMITED
TOTAL ALLOWABLE BUILDING AREA = UNLIMITED
ALLOWABLE AREA PER FLOOR = UNLIMITED
NUMBER OF STORIES = UNLIMITED

SECTION 406 - MOTOR-VEHICLE RELATED OCCUPANCIES
SEC 406.2.1 CLASSIFICATION - "Parking garages shall be classified as either open... or enclosed..."
GARAGES ARE ENCLOSED PER SEC 406.4.
SEC 406.2.2 CLEAR HEIGHT - "The clear height of each floor level in vehicle and pedestrian traffic areas
shall... comply with Chapter 11A or Chapter 11B, as applicable."
SEC 406.2.5 RAMPS - "Vehicle ramps shall not be considered as required exits unless pedestrian facilities
are provided. Vehicle ramps that are utilized for vertical circulation as well as for parking shall not exceed a
slope of 1:15 (6.67%)"
SEC 406.2.6 FLOOR SURFACE - "Parking surfaces shall be of concrete or similar... The area of floor used
for parking of automobiles... shall be sloped... Exceptions: 2. Floors of S-2 parking garages shall not be
required to have a sloped surface." GARAGE FLOORS WILL BE SLOPED TO CREATE RAMPS AS
ALLOWED IN SEC 406.2.5. SOME FLOOR ARES WILL BE FLAT.
SEC 406.2.7 MIXED OCCUPANCY SEPARATION - "Parking garages shall be separated from other
occupancies in accordance with Section 508.1" TABLE 508.4 WOULD ONLY REQUIRE A 1-HOUR FIRE-
RATED SEPARATION BETWEEN AN S-2 GARAGE AND B, M OR R-2 OCCUPANCIES (WITH FIRE
SPRINKLERS). PARKING GARAGE WALLS SHALL HAVE A 3-HOUR FIRE RESISTANCE RATING TO
MEET THE MORE STRINGENT REQUIREMENTS OF TABLE 602.
SEC 406.4 ENCLOSED PARKING GARAGES - BUILDINGS WILL BE CLASSIFIED AS ENCLOSED
PARKING GARAGE AND COMPLY WITH THE REQUIREMENTS OF THIS SECTION, INCLUDING THE
USE OF THE PERMITTED ROOF PARKING (406.4.1) AND THE PROVISION OF MECHANICAL
VENTILATION (406.4.2).

or portion thereof be equipped throughout with an automatic sprinkler system in accordance with this

SECTION 504 - BUILDING HEIGHT
SEC 504.2 AUTOMATIC SPRINKLER SYSTEM INCREASE - "Where a building is equipped throughout
with an automatic sprinkler system... maximum building height is increased by 20 feet and the maximum
number of stories is increased by one. For Group R-2 buildings of Type VA construction equipped
throughout with an automatic sprinkler system... the value specified in Table 503... shall not exceed 60 feet
or four stories." AUTOMATIC SPRINKLER SYSTEM INCREASE IS APPLIED TO BOTH BUILDING
HEIGHT AND ALLOWABLE AREA.
SECTION 506 - BUILDING AREA MODIFICATIONS
SEC 506.2 FRONTAGE INCREASE - NOT USED
SEC 506.3 AUTOMATIC SPRINKLER SYSTEM INCREASE - USED FOR HEIGHT AND AREA
INCREASES
SEC 506.4 (506.4.1) SINGLE OCCUPANCY BUILDINGS WITH MORE THAN ONE STORY - "For Group...
R occupancies... the total allowable area of a single occupancy building with more than one story above
grade plane shall be determined by multiplying the allowable area per story (Aa)... by the number of stories
above grade plan as listed below: 1. For buildings with two or more stories above grade plane, multiply by
2; 2. No Story shall exceed the allowable building area per story (Aa) as determined in Section 506.1..."

Aa = 36,000 SF

SECTION 509 - SPECIAL PROVISIONS
SEC 509.2 HORIZONTAL BUILDING SEPARATION ALLOWANCE - "A building shall be considered as
separate and distinct buildings for the purpose of determining area limitations, continuity of fire walls,
limitation of number of stories and type of construction..." A HORIZONTAL ASSEMBLY (CONCRETE
PODIUM) HAVING A 3-HOUR FIRE RESISTANCE RATING WILL BE PROVIDED BETWEEN THE TYPE
VA, GROUP R-2 BUILDING AND THE TYPE IA, GROUPS A-3, B & M (MIXED USE) BUILDING BELOW.
THE BUILDING BELOW THE HORIZONTAL ASSEMBLY IS NO MORE THAN ONE STORY ABOVE
GRADE PLANE. SHAFT, STAIRWAY, RAMP AND ESCALATOR ENCLOSURES THROUGH THE
HORIZONTAL ASSEMBLY SHALL HAVE NOT LESS THAN A 2-HOUR FIRE-RESISTANCE RATING
WITH OPENING PROTECTIVES PER SEC 715.4. THE BUILDINGS ABOVE AND BELOW THE
HORIZONTAL ASSEMBLY SHALL BE PROTECTED THROUGHOUT BY AN APPROVED AUTOMATIC
SPRINKLER SYSTEM IN ACCORDANCE WITH SECTION 903.3.1.1.

PODIUM) HAVING A 3-HOUR FIRE RESISTANCE RATING WILL BE PROVIDED BETWEEN THE TYPE
VA, GROUP R-2 BUILDING AND THE TYPE IA, GROUPS A-3, B & M (MIXED USE) BUILDING BELOW.
THE BUILDING BELOW THE HORIZONTAL ASSEMBLY IS NO MORE THAN ONE STORY ABOVE
GRADE PLANE. SHAFT, STAIRWAY, RAMP AND ESCALATOR ENCLOSURES THROUGH THE
HORIZONTAL ASSEMBLY SHALL HAVE NOT LESS THAN A 2-HOUR FIRE-RESISTANCE RATING WITH
OPENING PROTECTIVES PER SEC 715.4. THE BUILDINGS ABOVE AND BELOW THE HORIZONTAL
ASSEMBLY SHALL BE PROTECTED THROUGHOUT BY AN APPROVED AUTOMATIC SPRINKLER
SYSTEM IN ACCORDANCE WITH SECTION 903.3.1.1.
SECTION 602 - CONSTRUCTION CLASSIFICATION
TABLE 601 - FIRE-RESISTANCE RATING REQUIREMENTS FOR BUILDING ELEMENTS - THE PRIMARY
STRUCTURAL FRAME, EXTERIOR AND INTERIOR BEARING WALLS FOR A TYPE IA BUILDING MUST
HAVE A 3-HOUR FIRE-RESISTANCE RATING. THIS INCLUDES THE PERIMETER WALL OF THE
GARAGE. OPENINGS IN SUCH WALLS WILL BE LIMITED PER SECTION 706.8 AND PROTECTED PER
715.4. ALSO SEE "FIRE-RESISTANCE RATING REQUIREMENTS FOR BUILDING ELEMENTS (TABLE
601)," THIS SHEET.
SECTION 707 - FIRE BARRIERS
SEC 707.3.1 SHAFT ENCLOSURES - see 708.4
SEC 707.3.2 EXIT ENCLOSURES - see 1022.1
SEC 707.3.3 EXIT PASSAGEWAY - see 1023.3
SEC 707.3.4 HORIZONTAL EXIT - N/A
SEC 707.3.5 ATRIUMS - N/A
SEC 707.3.6 INCIDENTAL ACCESSORY OCCUPANCIES - see 508.2.5
SEC 707.6 OPENINGS - "Openings in a fire barrier shall be protected in accordance with Section 715.
Openings in a fire barrier shall be limited to a maximum aggregate width of 25% of the length of the wall and
the maximum area of any single opening shall not exceed 156 sf. Openings in exit enclosures and exit
passageways shall also comply with Sections 1022.3 and 1023.5, respectively."
SEC 708 (708.2) SHAFT ENCLOSURES - "Openings through a floor/ceiling assembly shall be protected by
a shaft enclosure complying with this section."
SECTION 903 - AUTOMATIC SPRINKLER SYSTEMS
SEC 903.3.1.1 NFPA 13 SPRINKLER SYSTEMS - "Where the provisions of this code require that a building
or portion thereof be equipped throughout with an automatic sprinkler system in accordance with this
section, sprinklers shall be installed throughout in accordance with NFPA 13..." ALL BUILDINGS WILL BE
EQUIPPED THROUGHOUT WITH AUTOMATIC SPRINKLER SYSTEMS PER NFPA 13.

SECTION 508 - MIXED USE AND OCCUPANCY
AREA "A" OF BUILDING 3 IS CLASSIFIED AS A SEPARATED OCCUPANCY MIXED USE PER SEC 508.4 AS
FOLLOWS:
AMENITIES A = A-3 OCCUPANCY
RES AREA A = R-2 OCCUPANCY

ALLOWABLE AREA (A-3, TYPE IIIA): 14,000 SF
ACTUAL AREA (A-3, TYPE IIIA): 3,093 SF
ALLOWABLE AREA (R-2, TYPE IIIA): 24,000 SF
ACTUAL AREA (R-2, TYPE IIIA): 4,988 SF
(3,093 / 14,000) + (4,988 / 24,000) = .22 + .21 = .43 < 1

SECTION 1003 - GENERAL MEANS OF EGRESS
SEC 1003.2 CEILING HEIGHT - "The means of egress shall have a ceiling height of not less than 7 feet 6
inches."
SEC 1003.6 MEANS OF EGRESS CONTINUITY - "The path of egress travel along a means of egress shall
not be interrupted by any building element other than a means of egress component..."
SEC 1003.7 ELEVATORS, ESCALATORS AND MOVING WALKS - "Elevators... shall not be used as a
component of a required means of egress... Exception: Elevators used as an accessible means of egress in
accordance with Section 1007.4" THE BUILDINGS ARE 5 STORIES IN HEIGHT. SELECTED ELEVATORS
SHALL BE USED AS REQUIRED MEANS OF EGRESS AND SHALL BE SERVED BY EMERGENCY
GENERATORS.
TABLE 1004.1.1 MAXIMUM FLOOR AREA ALLOWANCES PER OCCUPANT
THE FOLLOWING SPACES ARE INCLUDED IN THE PROJECT:

SECTION 1005 - EGRESS WIDTH
SEC 1005.1 MINIMUM REQUIRED EGRESS WIDTH - "The total width of a means of egress in inches shall
not be less than the total occupant load served... multiplied by 0.3 inches per occupant for stairways and 0.2
inches per occupant for other egress components.
SECTION 1007 - ACCESSIBLE MEANS OF EGRESS
1007.1 ACCESSIBLE MEANS OF EGRESS REQUIRED - "Where more than one means of egress are
required by Section 1015.1 or 1021.1 from any accessible space, each accessible portion of the space shall
be served by accessible means of egress in at least the same number as required by Section 1015.1 or
1021.1.
1007.2.1 ELEVATORS REQUIRED - "In buildings where a required accessible floor is four or more stories
above or below a level of exit discharge, at least one required accessible means of egress shall be an elevator
complying with Section 1007.4." SECTION APPLIES. SEE SECTION 1007.4
1007.3 STAIRWAYS - "In order to be considered part of an accessible means of egress, an exit access
stairway as permitted by Section 1016.1 or exit stairway shall have a clear width of 48 inches minimum
between handrails and shall either incorporate an area of refuge within an enlarged floor-level landing or shall
be accessed from either an area of refuge complying with Section 1007.6 or a horizontal exit. Exceptions: 2.
The clear width of 48 inches between handrails is not required... in buildings equipped throughout with an
automatic sprinkler system installed in accordance with Section 903.3.1.1..." 3. Areas of refuge are not
required at exit stairways in buildings equipped throughout with an automatic sprinkler system installed in
accordance with Section 903.3.1.1..." BUILDING IS EQUIPPED THROUGHOUT WITH AN NFPA 13
AUTOMATIC SPRINKLER SYSTEM. ALL STAIRS ARE MIN. 48" WIDE (HANDRAILS ENCROACH AS
ALLOWED.)
1007.4 ELEVATORS - "In order to be considered part of an accessible means of egress, an elevator shall
comply with the emergency operation and signaling device requirements of Section 2.27 of ASME A 17.1.
Standby power shall be provided in accordance with Chapter 27 and Section 3003. The elevator shall be
accessed from either an area of refuge complying with Section 1007.6 or a horizontal exit. Exceptions: 2.
Elevators are not required to be accessed from an area of refuge or horizontal exit in buildings and facilities
equipped throughout with an automatic sprinkler system installed in accordance with Section 903.3.1.1..."
BUILDING IS EQUIPPED THROUGHOUT WITH AN NFPA 13 AUTOMATIC SPRINKLER SYSTEM.
SECTION 1014 - EXIT ACCESS
SEC 1014.3 COMMON PATH OF EGRESS TRAVEL - "In occupancies other than Groups H-1, H-2 and H-3,
the common path of egress travel shall not exceed 75 feet. For common path of egress travel in Group A
occupancies... see Section 1028.8. Exceptions: 1. "Common path... in Group B, F and S shall not be more
than 100 feet provided that the building is equipped with an automatic sprinkler system... 2. Where a tenant
space in Group B, S and U occupancies has an occupant load of not more than 30, the length of a common
path of egress travel shall not be more than 100 feet. 4. ...in a Group R-2 occupancy shall not be more than
125 feet... with an approved automatic sprinkler system..." BUILDING IS EQUIPPED THROUGHOUT WITH
AN NFPA 13 AUTOMATIC SPRINKLER SYSTEM.

SEC 1015.2.1 TWO EXITS OR EXIT ACCESS DOORWAYS - "Where two exits or exit access doorways are

apart... measured in a straight line betwen exit doors... Exception 2: Where building is equipped throughout
with an automatic sprinkler system... the separation distance... shall not be less than one-third of the length of
the maxiumum overall diagonal dimension of the area served."

SECTION 1022 - EXIT ENCLSOURES

the floor assembly penetrated, but need not exceed 2 hours. Exit enclosures shall lead directly to the exterior
of the building or shall be extended... with an exit passageway conforming to the requirements of Section
1023..."

SECTION 1003 - GENERAL MEANS OF EGRESS
SEC 1003.2 CEILING HEIGHT - "The means of egress shall have a ceiling height of not less than 7 feet 6
inches."
SEC 1003.6 MEANS OF EGRESS CONTINUITY - "The path of egress travel along a means of egress shall
not be interrupted by any building element other than a means of egress component..."
SEC 1003.7 ELEVATORS, ESCALATORS AND MOVING WALKS - "Elevators... shall not be used as a
component of a required means of egress... Exception: Elevators used as an accessible means of egress in
accordance with Section 1007.4" THE BUILDINGS ARE 5 STORIES IN HEIGHT. SELECTED ELEVATORS
SHALL BE USED AS REQUIRED MEANS OF EGRESS AND SHALL BE SERVED BY EMERGENCY
GENERATORS.
TABLE 1004.1.1 MAXIMUM FLOOR AREA ALLOWANCES PER OCCUPANT
THE FOLLOWING SPACES ARE INCLUDED IN THE PROJECT:
Accessory Storage Areas, Mechanical Equipment Room:
300 gross
Assembly without Fixed Seats, Unconcentrated
15 net
Business Areas
100 gross
Exercise Rooms
50 gross
Mercantile
60 gross
Parking garages
200 gross
Residential
200 gross
SECTION 1005 - EGRESS WIDTH
SEC 1005.1 MINIMUM REQUIRED EGRESS WIDTH - "The total width of a means of egress in inches shall
not be less than the total occupant load served... multiplied by 0.3 inches per occupant for stairways and 0.2
inches per occupant for other egress components.
SECTION 1007 - ACCESSIBLE MEANS OF EGRESS
1007.1 ACCESSIBLE MEANS OF EGRESS REQUIRED - "Where more than one means of egress are
required by Section 1015.1 or 1021.1 from any accessible space, each accessible portion of the space shall
be served by accessible means of egress in at least the same number as required by Section 1015.1 or
1021.1.
1007.2.1 ELEVATORS REQUIRED - "In buildings where a required accessible floor is four or more stories
above or below a level of exit discharge, at least one required accessible means of egress shall be an elevator
complying with Section 1007.4." SECTION APPLIES. SEE SECTION 1007.4
1007.3 STAIRWAYS - "In order to be considered part of an accessible means of egress, an exit access
stairway as permitted by Section 1016.1 or exit stairway shall have a clear width of 48 inches minimum
between handrails and shall either incorporate an area of refuge within an enlarged floor-level landing or shall
be accessed from either an area of refuge complying with Section 1007.6 or a horizontal exit. Exceptions: 2.
The clear width of 48 inches between handrails is not required... in buildings equipped throughout with an
automatic sprinkler system installed in accordance with Section 903.3.1.1..." 3. Areas of refuge are not
required at exit stairways in buildings equipped throughout with an automatic sprinkler system installed in
accordance with Section 903.3.1.1..." BUILDING IS EQUIPPED THROUGHOUT WITH AN NFPA 13
AUTOMATIC SPRINKLER SYSTEM. ALL STAIRS ARE MIN. 48" WIDE (HANDRAILS ENCROACH AS
ALLOWED.)
1007.4 ELEVATORS - "In order to be considered part of an accessible means of egress, an elevator shall
comply with the emergency operation and signaling device requirements of Section 2.27 of ASME A 17.1.
Standby power shall be provided in accordance with Chapter 27 and Section 3003. The elevator shall be
accessed from either an area of refuge complying with Section 1007.6 or a horizontal exit. Exceptions: 2.
Elevators are not required to be accessed from an area of refuge or horizontal exit in buildings and facilities
equipped throughout with an automatic sprinkler system installed in accordance with Section 903.3.1.1..."
BUILDING IS EQUIPPED THROUGHOUT WITH AN NFPA 13 AUTOMATIC SPRINKLER SYSTEM.
SECTION 1014 - EXIT ACCESS
SEC 1014.3 COMMON PATH OF EGRESS TRAVEL - "In occupancies other than Groups H-1, H-2 and H-3,
the common path of egress travel shall not exceed 75 feet. For common path of egress travel in Group A
occupancies... see Section 1028.8. Exceptions: 1. "Common path... in Group B, F and S shall not be more
than 100 feet provided that the building is equipped with an automatic sprinkler system... 2. Where a tenant
space in Group B, S and U occupancies has an occupant load of not more than 30, the length of a common
path of egress travel shall not be more than 100 feet. 4. ...in a Group R-2 occupancy shall not be more than
125 feet... with an approved automatic sprinkler system..." BUILDING IS EQUIPPED THROUGHOUT WITH
AN NFPA 13 AUTOMATIC SPRINKLER SYSTEM.

SECTION 1015 - EXIT AND EXIT ACCESS DOORWAYS
SEC 1015.1 EXITS OR EXIT ACCESS DOORWAYS FROM SPACES - "Two exits or exit access doorways
from any space shall be provided where... 1. The occupant load of the space exceeds one of the values in
Table 1015.1. 2. The common path of egress travel exceeds one of the limitations of Section 1014.3."
TABLE 1015.1 - SPACES WITH ONE EXIT OR EXIT ACCESS DOORWAY
OCCUPANCY
MAX. OCCUPANT LOAD
A, B, M

SEC 1015.2.1 TWO EXITS OR EXIT ACCESS DOORWAYS - "Where two exits or exit access doorways are
required from any portion of the exit access, the exit doors or exit access doorways shall be placed a distance
apart... measured in a straight line betwen exit doors... Exception 2: Where building is equipped throughout
with an automatic sprinkler system... the separation distance... shall not be less than one-third of the length of
the maxiumum overall diagonal dimension of the area served."
SECTION 1016 - EXIT ACCESS TRAVEL DISTANCE
SEC 1016.1 TRAVEL DISTANCE LIMITATIONS - "Exits shall be so located on each story such that the
maximum length of exit access travel... shall not exceed the diatances given in Table 1016.1." DISTANCES TO
NEAREST EXIT NOTED ON PLANS MAY ALSO BE TO NEAREST EXIT ENCLOSURE OR EXIT
PASSAGEWAY.

SECTION 1021 - NUMBER OF EXITS AND CONTINUITY
SEC 1021.1 EXITS FROM STORIES - "All spaces within each story shall have access to the minimum number
of approved independent exits as specified in Table 1021.1..."

SECTION 1022 - EXIT ENCLSOURES
1022.1 ENCLOSURES REQUIRED - "Exit enclosures shall have a fire-resistance rating of not less than 2
hours where connecting four stories or more... Exit enclosures shall have a fire-resistance rating not less than
the floor assembly penetrated, but need not exceed 2 hours. Exit enclosures shall lead directly to the exterior
of the building or shall be extended... with an exit passageway conforming to the requirements of Section
1023..."
