The revised project proposes parking ratios consistent with the Specific Plan. Station Park Green is intended 
as a pedestrian-friendly, mixed-use, transit-oriented development, which offers the opportunity to share 
parking stalls between uses with different parking demand periods.
The approved project required the following (pursuant to Sec. 27.90.050 of the San Mateo Municipal Code):

The previously approved project included 781 residential parking stalls, which is three (3) more than the 
required number. With approximately 11,000 square feet of Office, and approximately 26,000 square feet of 
Retail/ Restaurant/Services, the previously approved project only required 57 non-residential stalls to satisfy 
the Zoning Ordinance. The previously approved project actually provided 131 non-residential parking stalls,

--- page 511 ---
which is 74 more than the required number. Of the 131 non-residential stalls:
•
20 will be reserved for 9,000 square feet of proposed Office space;
•
94 will be shared by the remaining 28,000 square feet of non-residential space;
•
12 will be reserved for loading;
•
5 will be reserved for public car-sharing services.
The current project proposes no change in the overall number of parking spaces. However, due to the change 
in uses, the number of required non-residential spaces has decreased.  Now, only 25 spaces are required in 
order to meet the development’s TDM program. In the Trip Generation Study developed by Hexagon 
Transportation Consultants, Inc., the proposed conversion of retail space to office space would generate fewer 
vehicle trips during peak hours. Furthermore, since Assembly Bill 2097 was signed into law, additional parking 
for residential and commercial uses is not required for a project within a one-half mile of a major transit stop 
(Hayward Park Caltrain Station).
E. ENVIRONMENTAL ANALYSIS
The following comparative analysis has been undertaken pursuant to CEQA Guidelines Sections 15162 and 
15164, to provide the City with the factual basis for determining whether any changes in the Original Project, 
changes in circumstances, or new information since the MND was adopted require preparation of a 
Subsequent EIR or MND.
The refinements to the previously approved projects are described in Section E (Project Description), above. 
The environmental analysis provided in the MND remains current and applicable to the Revised Project in 
areas unaffected by the refinements for the environmental topics, as listed below:
•
Aesthetics: The standard regulates projects that may have an impact on scenic vistas, scenic 
resources, or create a new source of substantial light or glare. The proposed amendment would not 
result in additional impacts to aesthetic resources beyond those identified in the MND, as there are 
no scenic vistas, resources, or light impacts on the site as the building has completed construction. 
The revised project does not change the structure configuration or overall building design. All changes 
to the tenant spaces are proposed in the interior of Building MU-1. 
•
Agriculture and Forestry Resources: The standard regulates projects located on prime or unique 
farmland, farmland of statewide importance, land zoned for agriculture, or forested land. The 
proposed refinements would not result in additional impacts to agriculture or forestry beyond those 
identified in the MND because there are no prime, unique, or statewide important farmlands in the 
project study area. The MND did not identify any impacts to agricultural uses; therefore, mitigation 
was not required. No new mitigation measures are required for the revised project, either.
•
Air Quality: The standard regulates projects that conflict with an air quality plan, would result in a 
considerable increase of pollutants, expose sensitive receptors to substantial pollution 
concentrations, or result in other emissions that would adversely affect people. The proposed 
refinements would not result in additional impacts to air quality beyond those identified in the MND. 
The background conditions, construction, equipment mix, and works hours identified in the MND 
have not changed significantly, and the proposed refinements would not result in any operational 
changes to the project once constructed.  Therefore, as described in the MND, the project would not 
exceed any Bay Area Air Quality Management District (“BAAQMD”) standards or contribute to air 
quality deterioration beyond BAAQMD projections. No new mitigation measures are required for the 
proposed refinements. The proposed amendment would not trigger a substantial increase in

--- page 512 ---
pollutants, as future work to the building will primarily be in the interior of the structure. 
•
Biological Resources: The standard regulates projects that would have substantial effect on animal 
species, habitats, wetlands or marshlands, wildlife corridors, or have any other impact on established 
conservation plans. The proposed refinements would not result in additional impacts to biological 
resources beyond those identified in the MND would not increase impacts to biological resources, 
either directly or indirectly. The structure is existing, and there are no hydrological resources or 
otherwise protected animal habitats on the site. No new mitigation measures are required for the 
proposed refinements.
•
Cultural Resources: The standard regulates projects that may impact historic resources, archeological 
resources, or disturb human remains. The Site is located in a “low-sensitivity” archaeology zone, and 
there are no known historic resources located at the Site. The project does not propose any site 
disturbances that may impact potential cultural resources, as the proposed project would effect the 
interior of the existing structure. No new mitigation measures are required for the proposed 
refinements.
•
Energy: The standard regulates projects that would create environmental impacts due to wasteful, 
inefficient, or unnecessary consumption of resources or would otherwise obstruct a state or local plan 
for renewable energy efficiency. The proposed amendment would not result in wasteful or inefficient 
energy consumption as the office uses would not increase energy use intensity. No new mitigation 
measures are required. 
•
Geology and Soils: The standard regulates projects that may be impacted from earthquakes, soil 
erosion, or located on soils are unstable or otherwise cannot support the structure. The proposed 
refinements would not result in substantially different geophysical impacts beyond those identified 
in the MND. The project does not propose any grading or other impacts to the soil, as the amendment 
would impact interior construction of an existing building. No new mitigation measures are required 
for the proposed refinements.
•
Greenhouse Gas Emissions: The standard regulates projects that may significantly impact the 
environment or conflict with an applicable plan or policy that reduces greenhouse gases, The project 
does not impact greenhouse gas emissions due to the proposed amendment or construction. 
Accordingly, the proposed refinements would not result in an increase in greenhouse gas emissions 
or related impacts to global climate change or conflicts with applicable climate change plans, policies, 
or regulations. Additionally, due to the reduction of retail, there is an estimated net reduction of 
vehicle trips that would lower greenhouse gas emissions to the site. No new mitigation measures are 
required for the proposed refinements. 
•
Hazards and Hazardous Materials: The standard regulates projects that would create a significant 
hazard to the public, emit hazardous materials, be on a hazardous materials site, or impact emergency 
response plans. The proposed project would not increase risks related to hazards or hazardous 
materials relative to the previously approved projects. The prior project mitigated potential hazards 
associated with removal of underground storage tanks as well as asbestos-containing materials, lead-
based paint residues, mercury and PCB-based materials, as applicable. For the current project, the 
proposed amendment would not increase the spread of hazardous materials or waste. No new 
mitigation measures are required for the proposed refinements.
•
Hydrology and Water Quality: The standard regulates projects that may degrade onsite water quality,

--- page 513 ---
interfere with groundwater recharge, substantially impact drainage, or otherwise obstruct the 
implementation of a water quality control plan. The proposed project does not impact hydrology and 
water quality requirements, and future interior construction shall comply with all applicable water-
quality regulations. No new mitigation measures are required for the proposed refinements.
•
Land Use and Planning: The standard regulates projects that would divide an established community 
or cause a significant environmental impact due to a conflict with a land use plan, policy, or regulation. 
The proposed project would not divide an established community. The project will meet the same 
land use and planning goals, objectives, and policies as the studied and approved previously, in 
addition to meeting the goals and policies in the subsequently adopted General Plan 2040 (including 
Land Use Policy LU 3.2, Commercial Development; LU 3.10, Office Park Evolution; LU 3.9, Workplaces; 
and Community Design and Historic Preservation Policy CD 8.2, Human-Scale Design). The project still 
proposes to implement a Transportation Demand Management (“TDM”) Program that would meet 
the requirements of the Rail Corridor Plan, as well as the previously approved projects’ combined 
Conditions of Approval & Mitigation Monitoring Plan.
•
Mineral Resources: The standard regulates projects that would result in a loss of the availability of a 
valuable known mineral resource. The proposed refinements would not result in additional impacts 
to mineral resources beyond those identified in the MND, and because the Site is not located within 
an area of known mineral resources, either of regional or local value, the MND did not identify any 
impacts to mineral resources; therefore, mitigation was not required. No new mitigation measures 
are required for the proposed refinements.
•
Noise: The standard regulates projects that generate a substantial temporary or permanent increase 
in ambient noise levels in the vicinity, generate excessive ground vibration, or impact an airstrip or 
airport. The proposed project would not result in additional impacts due to noise or vibration beyond 
those identified in the MND. The proposed refinements to the previously approved projects would 
not result in design or operational changes to the project site or surrounding area from that analyzed 
in the MND. The proposed amendment to allow for increase office uses would not generate a 
permanent increase in noise levels. No new mitigation measures are required for the Revised Project.
•
Population and Housing: The standard regulates projects that induce substantial unplanned 
population growth or displace existing housing or people. The amended project would not have any 
effect on population, housing, or employment in the City or region at large, as is the case for the 
previously approved projects. No adverse impacts would occur in this regard as the proposed 
amendment would not change the number of residential units on the site. No new mitigation 
measures are required for the proposed refinements. 
•
Public Services: The standard regulates projects that may result in an adverse impact to government 
facilities or impact public services. The proposed refinement to the previously approved projects 
would not result in additional impacts to public services/utilities beyond those identified in the MND, 
because they would not result in operational changes to the project beyond those evaluated in the 
MND for the original project. The MND did not identify any potentially significant impacts to public 
services; therefore, mitigation was not required. No new mitigation measures are required for the 
Revised Project.
•
Recreation: The standard regulates projects that may deteriorate nearby parks or would require 
construction or expansion of recreational facilities that might have an adverse effect on the 
environment. The proposed refinements will not result in additional impacts to recreation beyond

--- page 514 ---
those identified in the MND. The MND did not identify any permanent impacts to recreational 
resources; therefore, mitigation was not required. The proposed construction would not impact 
existing park resources, and the site contains an existing park that is not in the scope of work. 
Accordingly, no new mitigation measures are required for the proposed refinements.
•
Transportation/Traffic: The standard regulates projects that conflict with existing transportation or 
circulation plans, increase hazards due to design, or result in inadequate emergency access. A Traffic 
Impact Analysis (TIA) was prepared for the original project in 2010 and was included in the MND. The 
MND did not identify any near-term project-specific impacts to transportation/traffic and only 
identified that the project would result in cumulative traffic. In 2014, a TIA prepared by Hexagon 
Transportation Consultants for the stated that the revised project would not result in additional 
impacts to transportation/traffic beyond those identified in the MND. The report concluded that the 
TIA was expected to generate fewer trips that the original project. 
Hexagon Transportation Consultants provided a supplemental Trip Generation Study Report for the 
proposed changes to the office and retail uses on the site. The proposed conversion would generate 
197 fewer daily trips, including 14 fewer trips during the morning peak hour and 22 fewer trips during 
the afternoon peak hour.  The project does not propose any changes to the existing parking 
configuration, and the applicants have provided information that sufficient parking is provided for the 
change in use. Based on these findings, it has been determined that no new mitigation measures are 
required for the proposed refinements.
•
Tribal Cultural Resources: The standard regulates projects that may cause a substantial adverse 
change to a tribal cultural resource that is eligible for listing in local or state historic register or if 
evidence is found that a cultural resource exists on the site. The Site is located in a “low-sensitivity” 
archaeology zone, and there are no known cultural or historic resources located at the Site. No new 
mitigation measures are required for the project. 
•
Utilities and Service Systems: The standard regulates projects that require relocation or Constuction 
of new or expanded water treatment , drainage, power, natural gas, or telecommunications facilities, 
or otherwise impact water supplies, wastewater, or solid waste regulations. The proposed 
amendment would not require or result in the construction or expansion of any public utilities beyond 
those required for the original or previously approved projects. No new mitigation measures are 
required for the proposed refinements.
•
Wildfire. The standard regulates projects that would impact emergency response plans or are in a 
location that would exacerbate wildfire risks. The proposed amendment is not located within a High 
Fire Hazard Severity Zone and would not increase the risk of wildfire. No new mitigation measures are 
required for the proposed project. 
•
Mandatory Findings of Significance: The standard regulates projects that may degrade the quality of 
the environment, substantially reduce wildlife habitats, or adversely impact humans. The potential 
impacts of the proposed project with regard to biological resources, cultural resources, and direct and 
indirect effects on human beings would be essentially the same as under the prior projects. As impacts 
under the project would be similar to or reduced relative to the prior projects, impacts would be less 
than significant in this regard and no mitigation measures are required.
F. CONCLUSIONS

--- page 515 ---
Based upon the information outlined above, the amendments to the Specific Plan will not result in any new 
impacts or increase the severity of any impacts previously identified in the MND because the updated use 
ranges allowed for the ground floor of Building MU-1 are within the ranges for office and retail uses that were 
originally studied and allowed in the Specific Plan adopted in 2011. Nor are there any previously infeasible 
alternatives that are now feasible. None of the other factors set forth in Section 15162(a)(3) [new information 
of substantial importance] is present. An Addendum is appropriate because the project will not result in any 
significant effects not discussed in the prior negative declaration; there are no effects previously examined 
that will be more severe than what was shown in the prior negative declaration; and no previously infeasible 
or considerably different mitigation measures were found to substantially reduce the significant effects on 
the environment. As such, an addendum is appropriate because none of the changes described in Section 
15162 call for a subsequent EIR (Section 15164(a)) and only minor technical changes are necessary (Section 
15164(b)). The City has prepared this Addendum to address the environmental effects of the Revised Project 
compared to both the previously approved and original projects.
The conclusions of the analysis in this Addendum remain consistent with those made in the previously-
adopted MND. Specifically, based upon substantial evidence in the light of the whole record:
•
No substantial changes are proposed in the previously approved project that will require major 
revisions of the MND due to the involvement of new significant environmental effects or a substantial 
increase in the severity of previously identified significant effects;
•
No substantial changes have occurred with respect to the circumstances under which the Revised 
Project is undertaken that will require major revisions to the MND due to the involvement of new 
significant environmental effects or a substantial increase in the severity of previously identified 
significant effects; and
•
No new information of substantial importance, which was not known and could not have been known 
with the exercise of reasonable diligence at the time the MND was adopted shows that:
o
The revised project will have one or more significant effects not discussed in the MND;
o
Significant effects previously examined will be substantially more severe than shown in the 
MND; and
o
No mitigation measures or alternatives previously found not to be feasible would, in fact, be 
feasible and would substantially reduce one or more significant effects of the Revised Project, 
but the Project Applicant declines to adopt them.
Based on the information provided above, the proposed amendments to the previously approved Specific 
Plan would not result in a measurable increase in any environmental impacts over what was previously 
analyzed in the MND and first addendum. No new significant impacts have been identified, nor is the severity 
of newly identified impacts substantially greater than the conclusions of the MND and first addendum. Based 
upon this substantial evidence, the Specific Plan Amendments would not result in a substantial change in the 
conclusions and analysis included in the MND. This second addendum shall be maintained as a part of the 
administrative record files at City offices.

PA-2025-048 Station Park Green Specific Plan and Design Guidelines Amendment
We just received Notice of Planning Commission Public Hearing for the subject project. 
 
We want to go on record with the following concern: 
 
In general, we have no issue with conversion of retail space to office space. It would be great to see a local 
coffee shop where Starbucks used to be. From the plan it looks like Beach Hut Deli and former Starbucks space 
are the only retail spaces left. However, the notice does not specify how many employees will be on site. Our 
concern is enough parking for employees. We live in 19th Avenue Park across the street from Station Park 
Green. We do not want to see employees parking in the neighborhood. 
 
Chris Kober did confirm via email on March 20, 2025 (see excerpt below), that Essex would address any 
parking issues, but I want to go on record with the City of San Mateo with our concern. 
 
"As to your question of parking, yes off-street parking garage spaces exist today in our project’s original 
construction.  They have basically been sitting vacant all these years just like retail stores have been 
vacant.  So that will be the office parking for our employees.  In the event that you or anyone else has any 
issue with our project you may reach out to me directly and/or contact stationparkgreen@essex.com to reach 
the apartment staff there." 
 
 
Thanks, 
Linda Tolosano

--- page 528 ---
CEQA Finding 
The Planning Commission recommends that the City Council finds on the basis of the 
whole record before it that there is no substantial evidence that the Project will result 
in any new impacts or increase the severity of any impacts previously identified in the 
Addendum to the Mitigated Negative Declaration (MND), originally adopted on 
February 2, 2015.  An Addendum is appropriate because the Project will not result in 
any significant effects not discussed in the prior MND. There are no effects previously 
examined that will be more severe than what was shown in the prior MND and no 
previously infeasible or considerably different mitigation measures were found to 
substantially reduce the significant effects on the environment.  As such, an Addendum 
is appropriate because none of the changes described in Section 15162 call for a 
subsequent EIR (Section 15164(a)) and only minor technical changes are necessary 
(Section 15164(b)). The City has prepared this Addendum to address the environmental 
effects of the Project compared to both the previously approved and original projects.  
Based upon this substantial evidence, the Project will not result in a substantial change 
to the conclusions and analysis in the MND.

--- page 529 ---
Recommendation
Planning Commission make a recommendation to City Council to:
• Adopt an addendum to the Initial Study/Mitigated Negative Declaration 
pursuant to California Environmental Quality Act Sections 15162 and 
15164, based on the Findings for Approval and Subject to the Conditions of 
Approval; and 
• Adopt a resolution to amend the Station Park Green Specific Plan and 
Station Park Green Design Guidelines to change the mix of floor area 
allowed for retail and office uses.

potential future tenants, making the "community center" easier to access, and writing a check to the city, 
I feel as though none of those do anything to address the fact that the rent in this complex is absurdly 
high, considering the fact that they do such a poor job living up to the promises they laid out when I and 
other tenants agreed to rent here. 
 
I'm sure if you talk to any of the tenants that actually live here they would much prefer a 5% rent 
reduction, as opposed to three additional overpriced fast casual dining opportunities in the area, and 
100 Essex employees fighting for parking near by. 
 
Appreciate your time.
